Speech by Yang Youren After Returning to China 157

International Resolution to Reduce Miners' Working Hours

No Division for China in This Re-election of Labor Director

Yang Youren, the labor representative from China to the 15th International Labor Conference of the League of Nations in Geneva, and his advisor Lang Xingshi, have returned to Shanghai on the Japanese Postal Steamship Company's ship, Zhaoguo Maru, from Marseille, France, after completing their mission. The ship arrived at the Japanese Postal Steamship Company's pier on Yangzi Road, east of the Waibaidu Bridge, at 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon. The Shanghai Publishing Industry Union and representatives from other unions, as well as friends and relatives of Yang and Lang, went to the pier to welcome them. After Yang and others went ashore, they returned to their residences to rest with friends. According to Yang, he told the Xin Sheng News Agency reporter about their participation in the Labor Conference. The Chinese delegation to the International Labor Conference included Zhu Maocheng, Jiang Lufu (Acting Envoy to Italy) representing the government, Yu Benren representing labor, Zhang Xianglin and Lang Xingshi as advisors, and Bei Songsun and Kong Qingzong representing capital, totaling seven people. They arrived at the meeting on May 28th. Bei Songsun, the representative of capital, did not attend the meeting because he was unable to participate. The meeting closed on June 18th. As a result of the meeting, it was decided to reduce the working hours of coal miners by a quarter of an hour from eight hours to seven hours and forty-five minutes. The working hours of women working at night were not changed. The age of non-industrial child laborers was set at under 18 years old. As for the re-election of the directors of the Labor Council, there were twelve government representatives, six labor representatives, and six capital representatives, totaling twenty-four people. No one from China was elected. The Chinese government representative was only four votes short. On July 9th, Yu and Advisor Lang returned to China from Marseille. Before leaving Europe, they also visited the Ministry of Labor in Germany and the famous German factories, Siemens and Krupp. In England, they also visited the British Parliament.

Publishing Industry Union

Establishment of the Zhonghua Book Company Office 158

Yesterday (August 7th) at 4:00 PM, the Zhonghua Book Company held a general meeting of members at the Zhonghua Book Company's main factory on Jing'an Temple Road to formally establish the Zhonghua Book Company Office of the Publishing Industry Union. The union had previously submitted a request to the higher authorities for approval and was notified that it had been approved for record-keeping. The General Manager of the Zhonghua Book Company was informed by letter, requesting that employees be allowed to leave work early so that members could participate. On that day, over 500 employees of the company participated. Representatives from the Party and government agencies, including Wu Jiaze from the Municipal Party Department and Gu Bingyuan from the Social Affairs Bureau, attended to provide guidance. All members of the board of directors and supervisors of the Municipal Publishing Industry Union attended. Guests included representatives from various unions, the Commerce Office, the World Book Company, and the Public Concession Police Department. Despite the heat, the members stood and waited in an orderly manner. At 4:00 PM, the meeting was officially announced, and Mei Yujin, Wang Jiping, Huang Zhuting, Tao Shunbao, and Yang Yinlin were elected as the five-member presidium, with Qian Fuhai as the recorder. Chairman Huang Zhuting reported the purpose of the meeting. Wu Jiaze, the representative of the Municipal Party Department, delivered a speech, stating that the Zhonghua Book Company Union had already been established in 1927. Why was it being organized again today? Because the government had not yet promulgated laws and regulations to protect labor organizations, and the workers' own solidarity was not strong enough, resulting in its invisible disappearance. He hoped that they would unite more closely in the future. Furthermore, the capital side often misunderstands that workers organizing unions is detrimental to the capital side. They do not know that although unions seek the welfare of workers on the one hand, they also strive for production based on the principle of labor-capital cooperation. Now, the government has promulgated various laws and regulations, and various organizations can be organized according to law. For example, the business community has chambers of commerce and trade associations. We in the labor community should join unions and have labor laws to protect us. Furthermore, the strength of the Zhonghua Book Company Office lies in all of you. Everyone should take responsibility and not give up. Gu Bingyuan, the representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, delivered a speech, stating that the Publishing Industry Union is currently the leader of all unions in Shanghai, because its members are a group of intellectuals. He congratulated them on their success in holding the inaugural meeting, hoping that they would unite and fight legally. On the one hand, he asked them to pay attention to increasing productivity so that the cultural cause could develop. Hou Dachun, the representative of the Publishing Industry Union, delivered a speech, stating that if our workers want to seek their own solutions, they should join the union. Perhaps there are a few workers who are not very clear about this, so I will explain in more detail to make you understand. The union's past work has been full of struggle and hardship. We have also made considerable efforts in supporting the government, such as overthrowing the Zhilu Army and clearing out the Communist Party. Furthermore, if there are capital-side running dogs who undermine the union for their own selfish gains, the union will punish them according to law, without showing any favoritism. You should also regard them as public enemies and not tolerate them. Finally, the representatives of the Commerce Office and other guests spoke in succession (speeches omitted). After the speeches, Mei Yujin and the other nine people were elected as executive officers, and Jin Enpu and the other four people were elected as alternate executive officers. They were sworn in on the spot. A proposal was discussed, which was a request from the Zhonghua Book Company employees to the capital side to improve treatment conditions, totaling eleven items. It was unanimously passed. The meeting adjourned at around 7:00 PM.

Employees of Inland River Steamships and Tugs

Affiliated with the Seamen's Union 159

Gu Songlin and Sheng Fuquan, directors of the Shanghai Inland River Steamship Union, believed that the nature of inland river steamships and tugs was slightly different from that of ocean-going steamships and sailing ships. In July, they submitted a request to the Central Government to formulate separate laws and regulations for inland river steamship employees' unions, or to determine the nature of inland river steamship crew members in the regulations of the Seamen's Union. The Central Training Department reviewed and determined that although the scope of inland river steamships and ocean-going steamships is different, their nature is actually the same. Therefore, their organization should belong to the scope of seamen. Furthermore, although tugs on small boats are civil ships, they are attached to the business of steamships and should not be included in the scope of civil ships. They should be merged with steamship crew members and organized together. The Organizing Committee of the Chinese Seamen's Union has complied with the order and notified them to follow it.

Commodity Inspection Bureau

Yesterday's Reception for the Silk Industry and Financial Circles 160

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry sent Miao Zhongxiu, director of the Raw Silk Inspection Office, and Dr. Li Yaobang to Japan last month to investigate the silk industry situation. They returned to China the day before yesterday. Yesterday, Zou Bingwen, director of the bureau, hosted leaders from the silk industry and financial circles of Jiangsu and Zhejiang at the Shanghai Bankers' Association to report on their trip. More than 20 people attended, including Zhang Gongquan, Chu Fucheng, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Yang Dunfu, Shen Yichen, and Qian Fenghao. Director Zou introduced Miao Zhongxiu to give a report, which briefly stated that the scope of this trip to Japan included: (1) the process and current situation of Japan's silk industry relief, as well as future plans; (2) preparations for the compulsory implementation of raw silk grading and inspection in Japan; (3) silk fabric inspection methods; (4) warehouse organization, etc. Today, what I want to tell you is the first item. Since July 1929, the price of silk in Japan has shown a downward trend. In November, the silk industry association decided to reorganize the Imperial Silk Company to accept 50,000 bales of raw silk at a price of 1,250 yuan per dan (called joint custody). At the same time, it was decided that work would be completely suspended in the second half of December and that 20% of production capacity would be suspended from February 1, 1930, to May 31, to provide relief. In reality, the Imperial Silk Company only accepted 14,000 bales, and the reduction in production was ineffective, and the silk market still showed no improvement. Therefore, in January 1930, further relief methods were sought, and the silk industry association decided again: (1) the silk stored by the Imperial Silk Company would be inspected and graded by the Raw Silk Inspection Institute, and those with grades above the standard would be able to increase their mortgage funds; (2) the previous agreement for the custody of 50,000 bales would continue to be implemented, and the right to sell the jointly held raw silk would be given to a special committee; (3) the Imperial Silk Company would bear the loss of 100 yuan per dan, and those requesting a mortgage would bear six months of storage rent and interest, and after six months, all expenses would be borne by the Imperial Silk Company. This decision still did not have much effect. In the spring of 1930, the government promulgated regulations to relieve the silk industry, stipulating that 30 million yuan would be allocated within five years to compensate for the losses of banks accepting raw silk as collateral. On March 8, the government decided to accept 150,000 bales (85,000 packages) of raw silk of standard grade and above at a silk price of 1,250 yuan per dan. By the end of March of that year, the Imperial Silk Company had collected 50,000 bales, and by June 10, the banks had also collected 150,000 bales, for a total of 112,000 packages of raw silk. In addition to the above plan of the government and silk merchants to jointly store raw silk to stabilize silk prices, the silk industry also decided to reduce working hours from eleven to ten hours. However, despite the above relief plans, silk prices continued to fall. By the time of the new cocoons in July, there was an accumulation of 134,000 packages of raw silk. In addition, the harvest of new cocoons in 1930 was abundant, and the silk market was even more sluggish. The silk industry association decided again: (1) to petition the government to extend the term of the silk industry relief regulations (the implementation period of the regulations was originally scheduled to end in October 1930) to June 30, 1932; (2) half of the 112,000 packages of raw silk mortgaged by the Imperial Silk Company and the banks would be sold domestically within three years, and the remaining half would be sold at 3,000 packages per month starting from March 1, 1931; (3) all silk factories in the country would suspend work in mid-March of the 20th year; (4) the relief reserve fund (originally set at 4.5 yuan per package of raw silk sold) would be increased to 7.18 yuan per package (7 yuan borne by the silk factory and 0.18 yuan borne by the broker). After the above decision, although work was completely suspended in mid-March, the factories increased their production rate in mid-April. In practice, this regulation was equivalent to being ineffective. Regarding the sales method, only 3,000 packages were sold in mid-May, and the proposal for continued sales was invisibly abandoned. This is the process of the Japanese government and silk merchants jointly relieving the silk industry. Currently, there are more than 40 silk factories in Japan, with more than 300,000 silk looms, producing more than 60,000 packages of silk per month, of which more than 40,000 packages are exported, and the rest are sold domestically. There is no concern about excess supply and demand. As for the stock of more than 109,000 packages of silk, although there is a proposal to sell half domestically and half abroad within three years, due to various political and financial reasons, it is unlikely to be sold immediately and is not a cause for concern. The following points should be noted in future plans: (1) starting in 1932, the government will compulsorily implement grading and inspection to reduce various difficulties in trade and seek uniformity in products; (2) the original various associations of the silk industry will be united to form a national silk association to concentrate the power of merchants and cooperate with the government to carry out various undertakings; (3) within three years, 5 million Japanese yen will be used to promote silk fabrics in the United States to increase raw silk sales; (4) the addition of silk factories will be restricted to reduce production; (5) although government expenses will be reduced, research expenses will still be increased to expand research work; (6) small-scale silk factories will be merged to reduce production costs and standardize quality. In 1923, there were 4,309 silk factories and 200,588 silk looms. In 1929, the number of silk factories decreased to 3,719, while the number of silk looms increased to 326,976. (7) Various research projects aim to reduce production costs and unify and improve quality. The development of the Japanese silk industry has three characteristics: (1) government promotion; (2) silk merchant efforts; (3) expert research. The crystallization of the work in these three aspects has created this magnificent silk industry. If China wants to develop its silk industry, it cannot be effective without the cooperation of the government, merchants, and experts. It is hoped that the central government will quickly establish a research institution and gather famous scientists and experts from all over the country to jointly study and solve China's silk problems, which is promising.

Lease Agreement and Bandit Prevention Issues 163

The Real Estate Association Sent a Letter to Local Real Estate Companies Yesterday

Based on the explanation of the Shanghai Municipal Council's reply

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to local real estate companies yesterday (7th), which stated: "With regard to the lease agreement, it is a mandatory provision of Article 5 of the Regulations for Punishing Bandits. Now that bandits are rampant and bandit dens can be found everywhere, if there is no lease agreement for the rented house, the property is at risk of being confiscated. For the sake of safeguarding the interests of the real estate industry, the Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Shanghai International Settlement to inquire about its opinion. The Council replied that 'Your letter of July 10, which suggests that tenants must provide a lease agreement to prevent bandits from mingling, has been received with respect.' The following solutions are respectfully submitted for your consideration: (A) (1) As tenants may not be able to obtain a valuable lease agreement, the Association should inform the principal tenants that they may not sublet the remaining houses without informing the landlord. (2) If a principal tenant sublets the remaining houses, even if they have complied with the previous provision, they must still be responsible to the landlord and declare that the status of the subtenant has been notified to the relevant police station for investigation to ensure that they are of good character. If there is any concealment, they will be subject to expulsion. (3) Principal tenants who rent new houses in the future must obtain a lease agreement and hand it over to the landlord for safekeeping. The landlord must hire staff to verify the guarantors one by one to prove that they are reliable and trustworthy. (4) If anyone with suspicious behavior comes to rent a house, they must be reported to the police. (5) Without notifying the landlord or their agents, the police and clerks may not rent out the houses directly. (B) The lease agreement must be prepared in duplicate, one for the landlord and one for the guarantor. If the lease is terminated and the guarantee is released, the two copies should be exchanged and canceled. The landlord should still keep the canceled lease agreement for reference. (C) The lease agreement should be handled directly between the guarantor and the landlord after being introduced by the tenant. If the tenant terminates the lease, the release of the guarantee should still be handled by the guarantor themselves, so that the guarantor can impose sanctions on the guaranteed party at any time. The so-called lease agreement is only for the purpose of providing a guarantee and has nothing to do with rent payment, etc. As for the tenant registration form, all police stations in the settlement have them and can be obtained at any time. If the Association wants to further study this issue, please send representatives to meet with the Chief of Police to discuss it. We are eager to hear from you, etc.' In view of this, in addition to sending representatives to contact the Chief of Police, we hereby request that you investigate and take note of it, lest you delay and regret it later. (The following is omitted.)"

Passersby Blew Whistles Madly

Police Shot and Pursued

Resulted in the Death of a Bandit

Tao Was Safe and Sound

Tao Rangqing from Chuansha, who lives on North Fujian Road, was in his car at about 8:20 last night when four bandits suddenly appeared and tried to kidnap him. Fortunately, the victim was alert and shouted loudly. Three Chinese constables from the Huizi Police Station happened to be passing by and arrived after hearing the news, and shot and killed one bandit. Tao also escaped safely. The details are as follows:

Four Bandits Tao Rangqing, 60 years old, made his fortune in real estate. He lives at No. 474, North Fujian Road, north of Qipu Road. At 8:15 last night, he planned to go out to watch a movie and took his own car, No. 3873, driven by his driver Sang Quangen. Chinese Constables Pursued The bandits panicked after hearing the whistle and turned to flee, but they still held box cannons in their hands. A Frivolous Remark Caused Death 169

Jiang Dezhong Died So Suddenly

Liu Ribin Caused a Death

Jiang Bicheng, 49 years old, from Funing, lives at No. 11, Triangle Street, Nanshi. He has a son named Dezhong, who is 16 years old. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00, Dezhong finished his meal at home and invited Liu Ribin from Yancheng, whom he knew, to go to the Youche Wharf in Pubin to bathe in cold water. Liu did not know how to swim, so he watched from the shore. Dezhong took off his clothes and jumped into the water to swim. While he was having a good time, Liu suddenly joked to Dezhong and said loudly, "The water police are coming!" in order to scare him. Dezhong was greatly frightened when he heard the sound and immediately rushed back to the shore. When he looked back, there was no movement, and he knew that Liu had deliberately frightened him. He was so angry that he scolded Liu to his face. Then, a verbal dispute arose, followed by a conflict. Liu then raised his hand and pushed Dezhong's chest hard, causing Dezhong to lose his balance and fall into the bamboo fence next to him. In a moment, he didn't say a word, and his face was pale. Ding Guitao, a volunteer police officer from the First Precinct of the First District, heard the news and rushed over. When he felt him, Dezhong had already died of exhaustion. He arrested Liu and brought him back to the station. During the preliminary trial by the director of the station, Jiang Bicheng, the father of the deceased, heard the news and complained about the previous situation, requesting redress. Liu Ribin, 18 years old, who lives at No. 12, Qingyan Workshop, and makes a living by pulling a cart, confessed that he had joked with Dezhong, who became angry and insulted him and slapped him in the face. He pushed him, and he fell to the ground and died, etc. Because the case involved death, he was ordered to prepare a document and report it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Yuan Asheng Suddenly Lost His Niece

Yuan Amei Was Induced to Flee

Tao Wushi Designed to Move

Lu Chunsheng Uncovered the Secret

Yesterday, the man hired a car to send her back, but she was afraid of being scolded by her uncle, so she asked Wushi to help her hide it. Today, Wushi hid her in a box and used the excuse of moving to move her out, etc. When questioned, Tao Wushi's testimony was vague. District Chief Wang, considering that the case was bizarre, prepared a document and reported it to the Judicial Section for review.

A Supplement to the Dada New Ship

Scheduled to Start on the 15th of This Month

The various ships of the Datongyang Company's Yangtze River Tongyang Class have recently felt insufficient to manage. Since the Daji Wheel was burned, the original engine was still in good condition. Recently, in the middle of March, it was actively rebuilt and has been completed. It was test-driven the day before yesterday, and the speed of the wheel was very good. In a week, it will be officially launched for the Tongyang Class. The information obtained from yesterday's investigation is recorded as follows:

Tongyang Class Wheel The Datongyang Company's Tongyang Class travels between various wheels. Recently, the Dahe, Daqing, and Dede wheels have been sailing continuously every day, from Shanghai to Yang and from Yang to Shanghai. Each round trip takes more than 70 hours. After the Daji Wheel suffered an accident, it was supplemented by the Hanping Wheel, which was designated to carry goods, to carry passengers and load goods. Since the Hanping Wheel was transferred to Nanjing in early last month, only three wheels have been traveling back and forth for the Tongyang Class.

Daji Rebuilt The Daji Wheel was contracted by the company to the Ruirong Shipyard and has been in operation for three months. All the ship's hull and cabins are built with iron plates. There are more than 50 rooms, and the total tonnage is more than 1,400. The net tonnage of cargo that can be loaded is more than 900. The ship can accommodate 8-900 people. The ship is 216 feet long and 36 feet wide. It has been completed. The car was changed in Songkou the day before yesterday, and the results were very good. The speed can reach 12 yards per hour, which is 3.3 nautical miles. It is said that the cost of rebuilding the wheel is nearly 200,000 yuan. The name of the wheel has been changed to Dayu.

Dayu Schedule Since the past month, only three wheels have been traveling back and forth in the Tongyang Class. The company has decided to add the new Dayu wheel to the sailing from the night of the 15th of this month and officially allocate it to the schedule.

Wharf Issues The wharves from No. 1 to No. 16 in the Hunan District must be repaired once every three years. This year is the repair period. The Municipal Public Works Bureau has hired workers to repair them. The Datong wheel停轮碼頭 is located between the No. 4 and No. 5 wharves in the Hunan District. Therefore, recently, due to wharf problems, passengers on various Datong wheels have to take boats to the vicinity of the wheel mark (buoy) for transfer to the wheel every night to load cargo and passengers. It is estimated that the No. 4 and No. 5 wharves will be completed in about three or four days. Therefore, the Dayu wheel will be able to board the wheel from the wharf when it sets sail on the 15th.

Li Maolin of Liangxi Hotel

On March 6th of this year, the Detective Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau intercepted seven robbers near the Siming Guild Hall in Xiaobeimen. However, one of the seven, Wang Yaoting from Wuxi, suddenly implicated himself in the assassination of An Zhendong, a patrol officer of the Fourth District of Zhabei, in December of last year, admitting to being the perpetrator and claiming that the mastermind was Li Maolin, the owner of the Liangxi Hotel on Hubei Road in the Public Concession. Details had been previously reported in this newspaper. After several court hearings in the Special District Court, it was determined that Wang's confession was untrue, and Li was released on bail. Later, the Public Security Bureau sent Wang and the other six to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for review. Wang still claimed that Li was the mastermind of the An case. The Military Law Office, for the sake of caution, repeatedly investigated and summoned Li to court for confrontation three times. Li went willingly each time. Yesterday was the third trial, and Qi Haitian, the leader of the Detective Team handling the case, was also summoned to testify. As a result, Wang's confession was vague. Li Maolin stated that Wang and his accomplices had stayed at the Liangxi Hotel for thirty to forty days, owing a large amount of room fees. Unable to pay, they were evicted and bore a grudge, falsely accusing him. After a lengthy debate, the military judge ordered Li and Wang to be temporarily handed over to leader Qi of the Detective Team to thoroughly investigate and report back to the Public Security Bureau for further review.

Shanghai Bank Recruiting Trainees 179

The Shanghai Bank's business has been booming recently, and the existing staff is insufficient. Although there are some highly educated individuals among those recommended, they are not familiar with the bank's operations, which seems less than ideal. Therefore, the bank has decided to recruit dozens of trainees. Applicants should have a high school sophomore level education or equivalent. Registration will be open every day from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM. After being accepted, in addition to studying and interning, trainees will receive a monthly stipend of twenty yuan. At a time when the problem of student unemployment is particularly serious, the Shanghai Bank's open recruitment of true talent provides an extra avenue for high school students with real skills and knowledge, which is a rare opportunity. However, due to the large number of applicants in the previous recruitment, this time, only those with a proper job recommendation can register, indicating a slight restriction.

Minutes of the Executive Committee of the National Medicine Trade Association 198

The Shanghai National Medicine Trade Association held its 27th Executive Committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Zhuang Meitang. The following resolutions were passed: (1) (Omitted). (2) Regarding the case in which the association was previously ordered by the Central Executive Committee to amend the conditions of labor-capital treatment in this industry, we should continue to urge the competent authorities to expedite the handling of the case. Resolved: The association will send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the Party and government agencies for prompt review and handling. (3) The association has now received approval from the Ministry of Industry to divide and organize the internal and external field clerks of this industry, with the internal clerks joining the union and the external clerks joining the association. Is this solution acceptable to the association? Resolved: Although this solution from the Ministry of Industry seems fair, the internal clerks of this industry are also commercial users who directly serve the store and have absolutely no technical skills or crafts. According to the law, it is actually impossible to organize a trade union. The association should prepare a document and present it to the Ministry of Industry again, continuing to strive for the goal of abolishing the trade union. (4) The association has repeatedly received reports from members Zidetang, Baoshengtang, Jishengtang, Taishantang, Zhang Hongji, and others that criminals have taken advantage of the opportunity to fill prescriptions at midnight, using counterfeit ten-yuan banknotes, and more than a dozen colleagues have been deceived and suffered losses. A prevention method should be devised quickly. Resolved: The association will publish an announcement in the newspaper and notify all its members and colleagues in the city to pay serious attention. (5) The association should immediately convene the annual general meeting of members for the year 1931. Resolved: The Secretariat will expedite the preparation of the various procedures for the meeting and then schedule the meeting. (6) Some members of the association often have the situation of owing donations and failing to pay. How should this be handled? Resolved: The association will prepare a letter and send a donation collector to collect all outstanding donations within one week, without allowing any delays. (7) Committee member Zhang Hongzhao and Si Kunsheng introduced Bao Chengliang of Dashantang to join the association. Please review the case. Resolved: The case passed the review, and membership was granted. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

I request that you publish this letter in the "Letters to the Editor" section to clarify the truth and avoid misunderstandings. Sincerely,

Yue Junying, Lawyer, August 7th,

Youth Garden

Yearning 203

"This is the latest style, please try it," a middle-aged shop assistant with a shiny head respectfully handed her a pair of snow-blue and white high-soled rattan shoes.

"I really like this style – it's just a bit too long." She slightly bent over, stepping her foot, clad in the new shoe, onto the velvet carpet, scrutinizing it repeatedly. Suddenly, a soft, cottony palm patted her shoulder, startling her, and she hurriedly turned around.

"Oh, Bi Lian, I wondered who it was – when did you arrive?" She gazed at her with a sincere, joyful, and slightly surprised look.

"Ah, how wonderful that we could meet here," Bi Lian said, holding her hand tightly. "Have you bought your shoes? Let's go outside and chat."

"Yes, this pair will do."

She picked up the shoe box and walked out of the department store with Bi Lian, turned along the cement pavement, and entered a Cantonese dim sum restaurant. It was about ten o'clock in the morning, and only a few people were scattered around the tables. They casually ordered some dim sum and started talking. Bi Lian told her many things, and then said, "Do you know? Uncle Pucheng passed away."

"Oh, he's dead... How could he die?" A cold, pale, and thin face seemed to float before her eyes.

"I heard he was spitting blood."

"Oh, spitting blood..." A bright red shadow of blood flashed swiftly before her eyes.

A severely cold winter, snowflakes flying chaotically in the air, the north wind beating against the glass windows like mad, making a pattering sound. The sharp wind, drilling in through the window gaps, carried snow dust and struck the patient's face. He immediately started shivering. He shrunk his face into the collar of his tattered overcoat, stretched out a bloodless hand, and tremblingly tucked the old velvet blanket covering his legs in tightly. This slight movement immediately caused him to cough raspingly.

"Uncle Wen, are you cold?" she said, looking at the patient with concern.

Uncle Wen nodded, coughing even more fiercely.

She gently closed the curtains, and the room was immediately shrouded in a gray shadow, presenting a desolate and eerie scene.

She slowly walked back to her original seat and sat down, gazing gloomily at the patient's gaunt face, lifeless eyes, constantly choking and coughing, twitching... She couldn't help but feel a throbbing in her heart, as if a terrible horror would descend immediately upon this gloomy environment, and as if blood-red long tongues, disheveled long hair, and giant palms were flying and flashing back and forth before her. She was so frightened that she dared not look at the patient anymore. "Why isn't Aunt here yet?" she murmured from time to time.

After a burst of violent choking, Uncle Wen's face turned even more frighteningly pale. He said in a weak voice, "Yi, look, there seems to be blood." She stood up hurriedly and looked into the spittoon, so shocked that she almost cried out. It was so fresh, so red, like it had just been dripping from a chicken's neck, filling the spittoon with a foul, bloody smell.

"Oh, there really is blood. Let's grind some ink and drink it," she said, trying her best to suppress her fear and stay calm.

Uncle Wen shook his head, and a terrible, life-despairing pain was revealed in his dry eyes. He sighed slightly and turned his face inward.

Matted hair, a few yellow and pale whiskers under his chin, an open mouth... Gloom, silence. She fell into a realm of terror again.

"Heavens, Aunt is here!" She heard the sound of the door opening. As she ran to the narrow, dark alley, she encountered a dark, small figure. He was wearing a wide-brimmed woolen hat, his chin deeply hidden in the fur collar of his overcoat, the brim of the hat pressed low, obscuring the upper half of his face. She looked closely and recognized him as Uncle Pucheng.

"Is Uncle Wen in? It's so cold, he wouldn't have gone out, would he?" he asked, taking off his hat and using a handkerchief to brush off the snowflakes.

"He's at home – but, he's very ill," she said, staring blankly at Uncle Pucheng, trying to find a hint of pity in his cold eyes.

"Hmph, ill..." He made a snorting sound from his nostrils, and the corners of his mouth curled up slightly. He didn't ask anything else and quickly walked into the room.

"Wen, how are you? You should remember, the appointment we made the other day," Uncle Pucheng said, opening his small eyes wide and sitting on the chair by the door.

"Ah, Brother Pu, look, I've been very ill these past two days," Uncle Wen said, furrowing his brow and struggling to sit up. "I really don't know what to say. I'm so sorry."

"Sorry... I'm tired of hearing that word," he said, shaking his head, taking out a cigarette from his pocket, and lighting it. White smoke escaped from the corner of his mouth, billowing and spreading. Soon, the room was filled with smoke, and Uncle Wen, stimulated by the strong fumes, began to cough and choke incessantly.

"Alas, Brother Pu, I understand your kindness to me – but, I'm poor and sick, what can I do?" Uncle Wen said, panting.

"Who isn't poor? You have to find a way," he said, opening his eyes wide and shaking his leg casually.

"Yes, when I get better, I'll find something to do, and I'll definitely pay you back first," Uncle Wen said, a terrible bitter smile appearing on his face. He seemed to know that this hope was just a vague and elusive illusion for him.

"Get better? Of course, that's what I hope. But," he said, exhaling a puff of smoke, "you should understand yourself, how far your illness has progressed – and how can I let you keep owing me? Do you understand what I mean?" he said with an impatient look.

"Heavens, how am I to atone for this?" Uncle Wen pressed his hands against his chest and let out a long sigh. Two bitter tears rolled down from the corners of his sunken eyes, followed by several rasping coughs, a lump of phlegm stuck in his throat, going up and down but unable to be expectorated.

"Consumption, consumption... What hope is there?" He murmured, standing up, shaking his head, and walking back and forth in the room, as if calculating something.

At this moment, she was completely immersed in an atmosphere of silence. She was stirred by a sorrowful, resentful, and uncontrollable impulse. She stared at Uncle Pucheng's face with disgust, hatred, and hostility, but he seemed to pay no attention at all.

"What, are you saying? Clothes can also be used as collateral," he said suddenly, his eyes darting around.

"Clothes? I have nothing left – only this," Uncle Wen said, trembling as he stood up from the reclining chair, his body swaying from side to side. He pulled out a tattered fur robe from under the reclining chair, which he had been using as a cushion, and sat down again, saying, "This is all I have left. If you want it, take it."

"What's this worth? It's not even enough for a month's interest," Uncle Pucheng said, holding the robe in his hand, folding it slightly, and tucking it under his arm. He looked around again and said, "What else is there? What are we going to do?"

"Half a month later, perhaps?" Uncle Wen said with a sigh.

"That's too long. I can't wait."

"Ten days, then?"

"Still not enough."

"Alas, you have to let me find a way," Uncle Wen pleaded with him.

"Three days, no later than that," he said, glaring maliciously at Uncle Wen, and left without waiting for an answer.

After Uncle Wen watched him leave, he just stared at the ceiling and sighed, "Consumption... consumption," he repeated in a low voice. His expression became terribly frightening. He seemed to have already seen Death standing before him. Pain, despair, the terror of death, and the longing for life flashed momentarily in his faded eyes (she was simply terrified to the point of tears, even though she was only twelve years old).

On the morning of the third day, Uncle Pucheng came to Uncle Wen's house again to demand payment, and said many unpleasant things. By then, Uncle Wen was no longer able to speak. Phlegm rattled in his throat, his eyes staring blankly. Soon, he took with him the final contempt and disgust that the world had given him, and exhaled his last breath.

This tragic and cruel image was forever etched as a deep scar in her memory, especially the cold, pale, and thin face of Uncle Pucheng.

"Oh, he's dead, he died spitting blood," she couldn't help but repeat.

Guidelines for the Youth Corner 204

(1) Articles should be on topics related to youth issues, news from domestic and foreign schools or students, casual essays, descriptions of school life, etc. There are no restrictions.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photographs of youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, performances, lectures, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements are all welcome, whether individual or group. Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(4) Each article should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Write horizontally, do not write carelessly, Western text should be minimized, if it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(6) Regardless of whether manuscripts are published or not, they will not be returned. If return is required.

(7) Do not use ink to draw illustrations, and do not use colored paper, you must use black drawings on white paper.

(8) Please indicate that manuscripts should be sent to the Youth Corner Editorial Department.

(9) Regardless of whether manuscripts are published or not, they will not be returned. If return is required, it should be stated in advance.

(10) Payment for articles is divided into three categories: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to illustrations and photographs. If there are special manuscripts, payment will be calculated separately.

Book Review

After Reading "War at the National Gate" 205

— Wang Tiehua

To mention Mr. Wang Guoan's "War at the National Gate", one cannot help but also mention Mr. Huang Zhenxia's "On the Longhai Railway Line". Indeed, "Avant-Garde Monthly" successively published these two great works, which made me feel the power of literature and moved me to tears. When I pick up my pen to write these thoughts after reading, my enthusiasm surges uncontrollably. Great is "War at the National Gate"!

Who says that Chinese troops are incapable of fighting the enemy? Who says that there are no glorious battles in the history of national humiliation? Before reading the main text of "War at the National Gate", please first look at a few sentences in Huang Zhenxia's preface—

"In the Sino-Russian Manchuria Incident—excluding the eastern front of Tongjiang Mishan, solely based on the battle situation of Manchouli Zhalainuo'er, the Chinese army used a total force of 15,000, 4 cannons, and 2 aircraft. The Soviet Union imperialists used a total force of about 50,000, 200 cannons, 30 aircraft, and 30 tanks. Although the result was defeat due to being outnumbered, the enemy army suffered heavy casualties."

In such a battle situation with such a disparity in strength, the outcome is obviously predictable, but the loyal and brave soldiers ultimately exhausted their last breath in battle, burying their bright flesh and blood forever at the national gate. Just the few words, "Goodbye... beloved national gate... your children are powerless, farewell," are a tragic and heroic affair. Mr. Wang Guoan, as a company commander, experienced all the hardships and struggles, with a body covered in blood and a stomach full of indignation, jumped out of the trench and wrote this great work of 60,000 words, which is naturally even more passionate and intimate. I can boldly say that whoever reads it will not be moved.

There have been a few war novels in China, but nothing as great as "On the Longhai Railway Line" and "War at the National Gate". The former is a record of revolutionary battles, the latter is an account of a battle in the history of national struggle. Due to the differences in facts, reading "War at the National Gate" after reading "On the Longhai Railway Line" makes it feel even more grand, worthy of singing, and tearful. In a weak and poor China, there was still this battle at the national gate, and in a weak and poor Chinese literary world, there is still this "War at the National Gate", both are remarkable and astonishing feats. This is probably not just my personal frenzy.

At the beginning of this article, Manchouli is first written, and the situation and conditions of Manchouli are described very clearly. From the very ordinary New Year's reunions of many officers, the red terror is introduced in the green wine and red lights of the banquet, along with ironclad evidence of the Soviet Red imperialists' disregard for peace and their atrocities. The clouds of war gradually tightened, forcing them to pick up their guns and defend themselves in a desperate battle, until they were exhausted. The entire story is full of tense battle conditions and raging flames, making the reader wish they could roar, dance, and rush into the enemy ranks just like the author.

During the group banquet, the regimental commander jokingly said that Company Commander Wan's wife, Liubo, was a Red Russian, which flustered Company Commander Wan. He wrote,

"I was savoring the taste of being surrounded by beauty when I suddenly heard the regimental commander ask me that, which made me stunned for a long time and didn't know how to answer. Everyone thought it was because I had too much wine, and Liubo (his Russian wife) also noticed that the regimental commander was calling me, she kept pushing me with her hand, I had to stand up and say very flusteredly,

"Report to the regimental commander, Liubo's family is very well-off, her parents temporarily joined the party because they couldn't bear the coercion of the Red Russians, I have investigated it very clearly, I hope the regimental commander can believe it."

But once the war machine was launched, many spies were lurking in Manchouli to carry out sabotage, assassinations, and intelligence gathering. Company Commander Wan still didn't expect that his wife Liubo was really a spy. As things gradually became clear and he himself became aware of it, Wan was suddenly dismissed from his post with a baffling charge of "unauthorized departure from the defense area." At the same time, the chief of staff sent him a pistol to ask him to resolve Liubo. In the end, in the midst of his children's affection, he ended the life of this wife-spy. He wrote this passage perfectly,

I held the Browning in my trouser pocket, turned on the safety, and quickly aimed at Maria (another female spy), at the same time I said in my mouth, "Hands up, quick, quick," I was looking at Maria, but Liubo suddenly took out a pistol from her pocket, before she leveled it, I felt a buzzing sound in my head like a pile of fire burning, my hand slightly to the right, aimed at Liubo, bang a shot, a flash of fire passed before my eyes, Liubo fell down, Maria was about to run, my heart moved, forget it, and with another wave of my hand, bang, Maria also fell down.

The street lights were flashing, and we were walking very fast, I felt a vague shadow of Liubo and Maria walking in front of me in the darkness, I was a little scared and sad in my heart...

After reading this description, the reader felt unusually happy, but his heart yearned like this, writing out the conflicting psychology of love and hate, private and public. But he was after all a good man,

I don't know why, it seemed that someone said in my ear, "You have won, your motherland has won," my spirit suddenly lifted a lot, and the national flag on the headquarters building also appeared in front of my eyes...

This twist made the whole article more vivid, I think readers will feel it, and Mr. Wan also in this twist, was reinstated and went back to the front line.

Red Russia's disregard for non-war covenants, and willingness to act

Page 20

Guilty of undermining peace, has now been seen by the world, but there is no justice and fairness in the world anymore, at that time, when the war machine had just started, our authorities were still calm, hoping for peaceful negotiations, but the result was that this chaotic situation was created, and the hot blood of millions of men was sacrificed under the Cossack's iron hooves, but the army lost ground. He wrote the following passage about the initial battle

It was probably the morning of August 16th, the east had just turned fish-belly white, and we could vaguely see many teams moving down the mountain on the mountain opposite our position, and as the sky gradually brightened, we could also see clearly that there were many cavalry and infantry (about 1,500 people) the vanguard cavalry had already crossed half of the river, and were advancing towards our position in a completely dense formation, we had already reported to the deputy brigade commander at this time, and all the soldiers on the entire line had also entered the position, because we had received an order from the brigade commander that no matter what, we were not allowed to shoot, at this time the brothers were all anxious and wanted to take advantage of their half-crossing to attack and annihilate the enemy in one fell swoop, but the order was stern, and everyone had to lie in the trenches and watch.....

Everyone who entered the position hated so much that they gnashed their teeth, and almost shouted out the sound of hitting, but the company and platoon leaders humbly comforted, "The order is important,"

When I read these connected paragraphs, I was so moved that my anger rose, thinking about how many mistakes the soldiers on the front line had made in this delay. There has never been justice in the world, only self-reliance can lead to fairness, at this critical moment, the authorities still tried their best to calm down, but they knew that their own land had been trampled by others. This situation, even we who were hiding far away, felt angry when we read the newspaper, let alone the author hiding in the trenches, and the writing was naturally even more angry.

But after a burst of fighting, the soldiers couldn't help but move forward like crazy, killing, killing, regardless of the fact that their own trenches had been flattened by the enemy's artillery fire, and their own brothers had already sacrificed 150 people in the first raid, and in the end, they drove the enemy back like a flood.

Our inflexible machine guns killed many enemies, and our soldiers were all happy to kill, if they didn't call out the brigade adjutant, they would all have crossed the river.

How strong was the morale at this time, the author drew out one red heart after another on the paper, I don't know how many people were moved, but the lone army was trapped, and there was no follow-up support, at the same time, the damned Feng Yuxiang, again took advantage of the crisis to rebel, and the brothers in front of the battle, so only waited for orders in a desperate defense, and the Red Russian's guns and iron hooves, continued to come without increase, alas, the sin of the soldiers,

He wrote a few paragraphs in Manchouli, which were really so magnificent

The gun was placed on the chest wall, and the food from the rear could not be sent up, everyone had to endure hunger, and wait for the enemy to stop firing before eating, but the shells kept flying, we firmly guarded, and never retreated one step, the brigade commander also sent an order, - our entire 15th brigade sacrificed together with Manchouli, whoever retreats first will be shot, this order was printed in our minds word by word, no matter how the enemy attacked, as long as we have one breath and one gun, we have to fight with the enemy...

Every minute and every second was spent in the enemy's guns and bullets, I watched one of my beloved brothers being killed by artillery fire, and two more were injured, two hours passed, my brothers were thirteen or fourteen injured, I was really a little crazy, I kept running up to stroke the dead body, fresh red blood flowed in the battle trench, and pieces of white brain splashed on the edge of the trench

Morning of November 17, 1918 of the Republic of China...

They jointly received the order from Commander Liang, - children, it is glorious and great to sacrifice for the motherland, you go and do it

After several consecutive waves of fierce attacks, the Red Cavalry was unable to succeed immediately thanks to the spirit of firm defense. Finally, the unfortunate record came,

"We had just celebrated the end of the storm when the enemy cavalry in front started attacking again, and the bullets killed almost all of the more than 5,000 knights, the bloodstains were left on the endless ice and snow, just as the gunfire stopped, more than a dozen enemy planes flew over and dropped bombs on the radio station, pop - pop pop, and the last radio telegram received, the radio station also collapsed along with the fate of the bomb,

Seeing "On this desolate, tragic and heroic evening, I received the order, - my battalion covers the retreat of my regiment, and the company covers the retreat of my battalion... The quiet night air also seemed to contain a sad component," there was a sense of gloom. "Finally, with a belly full of hot blood, they broke out of the encirclement of smoke and bullets, and looked sadly at the enemy's sickle and axe on the flagpole of Manchouli,"

At the end of the entire article, two letters recalling the loss were used as the ending, which I thought was very good. At the same time, it can be seen that the bold and sad feelings of the two soldiers are vividly expressed in the unadorned words, leaving their true colors.

In short, the entire article is 60,000 words long, and I can't cite more here. I think that although Mr. Wang Guoan did not die in battle, he still has these 60,000 words to atone for the crime of retreating from the war to the Chinese people. At this time when internal rebellions and external disasters are coming one after another, the people of the country should read this kind of creation carefully to stimulate the decline and excite the spirit. (I hope that those who are interested in domestic films should use this point to take material, its greatness should exceed "All Quiet on the Western Front" ten times, in a sluggish China, what is needed is this kind of theme of film,)

I also want to quote Huang Zhenxia's preface without fear of words

"The people hiding in the customs, the people in the big cities in the red lights and green wine, the people who are complaining in the pavilion room, the young people of China, do you still remember the shocking event of November 21, 1918 of the Republic of China, do you still remember 6,000 miles away, under the yellow sand and white grass or the snowy national gate, there were thousands of brave and sad northeastern heroes resisting the red terror, I am afraid that you have forgotten it completely, if you have forgotten it, please see "War at the National Gate,"

Finally, I repeat, "In a weak and poor China, there is still this battle, and in a weak and poor Chinese literary world, there is still this article," Here, I would like to pay tribute to the author,

How We Should Read 206

— Ke

Edited by Fan Shou Kang

My younger brother is studying at a middle school. Recently, he wrote a letter asking me to buy some books and send them to him.

Speaking of books, as long as we casually step into any bookstore, they are all "stacked like mountains." However, among this "vast sea of books," it is rare to find one that can provide accurate guidance to middle school students on how to effectively study all subjects.

We well know that "there are two essential elements to reading: first, be precise; second, be broad." If we want to achieve "precision" in a certain academic field, then we must first seek the assistance of "breadth" in knowledge. During middle school, if a solid foundation is not laid in various courses, it will be difficult to reach advanced peaks in specialized schools. Thus, we feel how important middle school courses are. However, if we can obtain the most convenient path to achieve the ultimate goal of learning, in terms of success, we can achieve twice the result with half the effort. Therefore, to promote middle school students' ease of understanding of their coursework, guidance on a method of study is urgently needed.

Finally, I discovered such a book, one that encompasses the study and methods of six compulsory subjects. It is a collection of works by specialists in various fields—and these works have been collected by the editor over many years in various aspects.

The entire book is divided into seven sections, each explaining how to start exploring a certain subject. The first section is on the purpose and method of learning; the second section is on how we should learn Chinese; the third section is on how we should learn mathematics; the fourth section is on how we should learn English; the fifth section is on how we should learn natural sciences; the sixth section is on how we should learn history and geography; and the seventh section is on how we should learn drawing and music.

The first section, "The Purpose and Method of Learning," contains six articles on being a person and "seeking knowledge," and each article contains precise enlightenment. This section can be regarded as the introduction to the entire book. "Learning and Being a Person" is a piece of literature full of philosophy. It answers the questions of "why study" and "the meaning of studying and being a person" very thoroughly. "Why Study and How to Study" and "Methods and Materials for Learning" comprehensively and thoroughly reveal the necessary preparatory steps for studying and the results of research by scholars from the East and West over the past sixty years on different materials. In a section of "Why Study and How to Study," the explanation of "learning" and "student" is particularly precise. It says,

"If humanity has no learning, humanity cannot survive. If humanity has no learning, humanity has no need to survive—a world that never evolves, barren and monotonous, what pleasure is there in living in it? Therefore, I say, one must learn throughout life, and learning is life."

The second section, "How We Should Learn Chinese," also contains six works by experts in Chinese studies. The first four articles explain the research methods and basic knowledge of writing in Chinese studies. The last two articles list a reading list for learners.

The third section, "How We Should Learn Mathematics," explains the function of mathematics and its relationship to human life, as well as the habit of "seeking truth" that should be cultivated when studying mathematics, and the methods of entry. It contains an article "A Path to Instructing Young People in the Study of Geometry," which dissects the meaning of geometry and the theorems of deduction especially finely. The last article is "Introducing Several Excellent Arithmetic Books to Middle School Students," with a list of thirty-five kinds, all of which are practical arithmetic textbooks.

The fourth section, "How We Should Learn English," here, there is only one article, "Methods of Learning English," and "Introducing Twenty Kinds of English Magazines." However, regarding the grammar, reading, spelling, writing, and necessary books for beginners in English, there is already very detailed guidance.

The fifth section, "How We Should Learn Natural Sciences," explains the interest aroused by studying natural sciences, and the methods of learning natural sciences and experimentation. This section has five articles, precise discussions, all of which are works by experts in science.

The sixth section, "How We Should Learn History and Geography," this section has detailed descriptions of the concept of history, the collection of historical materials, and research methods. "Historical Research Methods" can especially correct and reform general old history studies, with detailed concerns about the tendencies taken by new history studies. The important relationship between geography and humanity, and the steps of learning, and the definition of geography, are also explained very thoroughly.

The seventh section, "How We Should Learn Drawing and Music," here there are five works. It clearly reveals to us the meaning of art, and the happiness and pleasure it gives to humanity, and the foundation of preparation, one by one, so that readers naturally develop a love of art.

This book meets the needs of middle school students and is a major contribution to the academic community. Friends who are determined to study, this is a shortcut to learning that the editor, Mr. Fan, has newly opened up for you.

French General Foch's War Diaries 207

— Translated by Gu Angruo

The sixteenth was calm and uneventful. The German attack failed the day before yesterday, and there can be no good development now. On the Xiangben front, the German offensive has reached the end of its strength.

South of the Marne River, the enemy army failed to deploy the defense line guarding the bridgehead. What the enemy army encountered was not only stubborn defense, but also the fierce counterattack of the French Sixth Army, preventing enemy troops everywhere, and even recapturing several important towns. If our artillery and air force continue to bombard the Marne River bridges, making it difficult for the enemy to resupply reinforcements and ammunition, the bottom of the enemy's pocket-shaped position in the Thierry area will inevitably fall into danger.

The only progress the enemy army made on the sixteenth was southwest of Reims, between the Vesle River and the Marne River, especially along the Marne River. However, this progress was local and insignificant to the overall situation, and it was difficult to advance further at the cost of great sacrifices.

After using two days of strength in the hope of salvaging the uncertain gains on the Marne River, there was no result. The German High Command must be hesitant. The enemy once shouted, "Fight and win to see peace again." What is the result? Nothing but resentment, deceit, and a harbinger of failure. The morale of the entire army will inevitably be greatly affected by this.

On July 17, the German army was already in a slump. On the 18th, the allied artillery bombarded like thunder at the predetermined time and place.

As previously mentioned, as early as June, I had noticed the importance of Soissons to the enemy army, because its location is a railway center, which is absolutely indispensable for the supply of the deep and isolated army in the Thierry area. Its location is not far from our front line. Taking an offensive towards this city, preparations have now begun according to my plans of June 14 and June 16. Commander Mangin's operational plan was also completed on June 20. Since that time, I have thought that the result of our army's counterattack, shifting from west to east, must be greater than merely disrupting the enemy's transportation.

Commander Mangin then gradually expanded his plan to include the fifteen-mile area from his defense line on the Aisne River to the point where he connects with the left wing of the French Sixth Army on the Ourcq River. His forces were also increased to eighteen infantry divisions (including the American First and Second Divisions), three cavalry divisions, two hundred and forty 75mm guns, two hundred and thirty-one heavy guns, forty-one air squadrons, and three hundred and seventy-five tanks.

Commander Degoutte of the Sixth Army reported that he would extend the Tenth Army to the right, and the planned battle would extend to the other side of the Ourcq River. He could also operate in the same way. He had already drafted a plan for the Sixth Army to launch another offensive along the Ourcq-Clignon line, with the Tenth Army attacking on its left wing. He wanted a tank unit and one or two infantry divisions under his command. After the increase in forces, he had a total of eight divisions of troops for combat. The offensive line could be expanded by sixteen miles.

On July 9, I also thought of the Fifth Army launching a simultaneous offensive westward on the line from Reims to the Marne River. However, since that time, the situation of the Fifth Army has changed, and it can now only undertake secondary military tasks.

At that time, the bases from which the Tenth and Sixth Armies set out had greatly improved after several wars. West of Soissons, the Tenth Army had established a position on the plateau from Cœuvres to Dommiers. Further south, the Tenth Army had seized the two villages of Longpont and Corcy, which are adjacent to the Retz Forest. Its vanguard had advanced east of the Savières stream. West of Thierry, the Sixth Army recaptured several important towns, such as the villages of Vaux. The American Second Division performed very well.

In order to salvage the critical situation, the German High Command had obviously divided its army into two parts, one to guard the western war zone and the other to seize new territory to the south. The forces of the two parts were not very equal to each other.

When the German army's general offensive failed and it was in a slump, the prospects for our army's counterattack and the achievements already made were roughly like this. (To be continued)
